# LoCoBench-Agent Task

## Task Information

**Task ID**: rust_api_microservice_expert_008_architectural_understanding_expert_01
**Category**: architectural_understanding
**Difficulty**: expert
**Language**: rust
**Context Length**: 1014465 tokens
**Files**: 85

## Task Title

Architectural Analysis and Redesign for Cache Invalidation in a Rust Microservice

## Description

LedgerLink Nexus is a high-performance Rust-based financial data API microservice. To handle high read loads, the system implements a sophisticated response caching layer. A critical bug report has emerged: clients are intermittently receiving stale data for resources that have been recently updated. This issue persists until the cache entry's Time-To-Live (TTL) expires. As a senior architect, your task is to analyze the system's architecture, pinpoint the root cause of this data consistency problem, and propose a robust architectural solution.

## Your Task

You are tasked with resolving a critical stale data issue in the LedgerLink Nexus service. Your analysis and proposal should be based entirely on the provided source files.

1.  **Analyze the System**: Examine the provided source code to understand the overall architecture. Given the obfuscated filenames, you must infer the purpose of each module from its content.
2.  **Identify Key Components**: Pinpoint the specific modules responsible for the following functions:
    *   a) The core response caching logic.
    *   b) Handling incoming read requests (e.g., `GET` operations).
    *   c) Handling incoming write requests (e.g., `POST`, `PUT`, `DELETE` operations).
3.  **Diagnose the Flaw**: Clearly describe the fundamental architectural flaw that causes the stale data issue. Explain *why* updating a resource does not immediately reflect in subsequent read requests.
4.  **Propose a Solution**: Design an architectural solution to ensure cache consistency. Do not write the full implementation. Instead, describe the design pattern you would employ (e.g., explicit invalidation, write-through caching). Justify your choice.
5.  **Outline Implementation Plan**: List the specific modules that would require modification to implement your proposed solution. Describe the new interactions that must be established between these modules (e.g., which module calls which, and with what information).

## Expected Approach

An expert developer would approach this task systematically:

1.  **Initial Reconnaissance**: The developer would start by inspecting `package.json` to identify the web framework (e.g., `actix-web`, `axum`) and caching libraries (e.g., `redis`, `moka`). They would then review `src/config.txt` to find configuration parameters related to caching (like TTLs, Redis connection strings) and other services.
2.  **Trace Request Lifecycle**: The next step is to find the application's entry point (e.g., a `main` function initializing the server). This would reveal the middleware pipeline, providing clues about the modules responsible for logging, authentication, and caching.
3.  **Module Identification via Keywords & Patterns**:
    *   **Caching Module**: The developer would search across all `src/*.txt` files for keywords like `cache`, `redis`, `get`, `set`, `ttl`, and patterns related to the identified caching library. This would lead them to the module(s) encapsulating caching logic.
    *   **Handler Modules**: They would search for web framework macros or function signatures that define routes (e.g., `#[get("/...")]`, `#[post("/...")]`, `web::resource(...).to(...)`). This would identify the modules handling HTTP requests.
    *   **Distinguish Read/Write**: Within the handler modules, the developer would differentiate between read (`GET`) and write (`POST`, `PUT`, `DELETE`) operations based on the HTTP method specified in the route definition.
4.  **Connect the Dots & Identify the Flaw**: The developer would trace the logic for a typical `GET` request, noting its interaction with the caching module (a `cache.get()` call). Then, they would trace a `PUT` or `POST` request for a similar resource, observing that while it interacts with a database or data source, it makes *no corresponding call* to the caching module to update or invalidate the now-stale entry. This absence of interaction is the core architectural flaw.
5.  **Formulate the Architectural Fix**: The developer would propose a direct cache invalidation strategy. They would suggest modifying the write handlers to explicitly call an `invalidate(key)` or `delete(key)` function on the caching service after a successful database write. They would justify this as a robust, immediate, and targeted solution, superior to simply lowering the cache TTL.
6.  **Plan the Changes**: Finally, they would specify that the identified write-handler module(s) need to be changed to call a new function in the identified caching module. The plan would detail that the write handler needs to construct the correct cache key (the same key the `GET` handler uses) and pass it to the new invalidation function.

## Evaluation Criteria

- **Component Identification Accuracy**: Did the agent correctly identify the primary modules for caching, read handling, and write handling (`module_44`, `module_26`/`52`, `module_71`)?
- **Flaw Diagnosis Clarity**: Was the agent able to articulate that the problem is the *absence of an invalidation signal* from the write handlers to the cache, rather than a bug in the caching logic itself?
- **Solution Robustness**: Did the agent propose a robust architectural pattern like explicit invalidation? Points are deducted for simplistic or ineffective solutions like 'just lower the cache TTL'.
- **Implementation Plan Correctness**: Did the agent correctly identify that both the write handler module and the caching service module require modification?
- **Interaction Description**: Did the agent clearly describe the new required interaction: the write handler calling an invalidation function in the cache service after a successful DB write?
- **Reasoning Quality**: Does the agent's justification for its proposed solution demonstrate an understanding of trade-offs in distributed systems (e.g., consistency vs. performance)?

96-assistanttext-
I have completed the architectural analysis task. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Summary

**Primary Finding**: The stale data issue in LedgerLink Nexus is caused by the **absence of cache invalidation signals** from write handlers to the Redis response cache.

### Key Components Identified

1. **Caching Modules**:
   - `module_9.txt` - Core ResponseCache with `purge_namespace()` method (lines 185-196)
   - `module_44.txt` - Ledger Entry listing with Redis response caching
   - `module_72.txt` - Pagination + Response Caching facade with `purge()` method

2. **Read Handlers (GET operations)**:
   - `module_26.txt` - Actix-web endpoint `#[get("/api/v1/ledger/entries")]`
   - `module_52.txt` - High-frequency paginated read-model with caching
   - `module_44.txt` - Axum-based `list_ledger_entries_handler`

3. **Write Handlers (INSERT/UPDATE)**:
   - `module_38.txt` - Contains `insert()` method that writes to DB **without cache invalidation** (this is the core flaw)

### Root Cause

The write handlers (like `insert()` in module_38) successfully commit database transactions but **do not call any cache invalidation method**. The caching infrastructure (`purge_namespace()` in module_9) exists specifically for this purpose but is never invoked by write operations.

### Proposed Solution

**Explicit Cache Invalidation Pattern**: After each successful database write, the write handler must explicitly call the cache service to invalidate affected entries.

Required modifications:
1. **Write handler modules** (module_38) - Add cache service dependency and call invalidation after DB commits
2. **Cache service modules** (module_9, module_72) - Already have invalidation methods; ensure they're accessible to write handlers

The solution was documented in `/logs/agent/solution.md` w
... (truncated)

Example:\n//! ```no_run\n//! let cfg = ledgerlink_nexus::config::get();\n//! tracing::info!(bind = ?cfg.http.bind, \"\ud83d\ude80  HTTP server starting\");\n//! ```\n\nuse std::{net::IpAddr, path::Path, sync::Arc, time::Duration};\n\nuse config::{Config, ConfigError, Environment, File};\nuse once_cell::sync::OnceCell;\nuse secrecy::{ExposeSecret, SecretString};\nuse serde::Deserialize;\nuse thiserror::Error;\n\n/// Retrieve the global, lazily-initialised [`AppConfig`].\n///\n/// # Panics\n/// The function panics if configuration loading fails **once** at startup.\n/// Subsequent calls are guaranteed not to panic.\npub fn get() -> &'static AppConfig {\n    static INSTANCE: OnceCell<AppConfig> = OnceCell::new();\n    INSTANCE.get_or_init(|| match AppConfig::load() {\n        Ok(cfg) => cfg,\n        Err(e) => {\n            // A config load failure is considered unrecoverable.\n            eprintln!(\"\u274c Failed to load configuration: {:?}\", e);\n            std::process::exit(1);\n        }\n    })\n}\n\n/// Shallow clone wrapper around [`get`].\n/// Useful when configuration needs to be shared across async tasks.\npub fn shared() -> Arc<AppConfig> {\n    Arc::new(get().clone())\n}\n\n/// Complete application configuration (root).\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)]\n#[serde(rename_all = \"snake_case\")]\npub struct AppConfig {\n    pub http: HttpConfig,\n    pub postgres: PostgresConfig,\n    pub redis: RedisConfig,\n    pub auth: AuthConfig,\n    pub pagination: PaginationConfig,\n    pub caching: ResponseCacheConfig,\n    pub logging: LoggingConfig,\n}\n\nimpl AppConfig {\n    /// Load configuration from the following sources **in order**:\n    ///  1. `config/default.{toml,yaml,json}` (optional)\n    ///  2. `config/{RUN_MODE}.{toml,yaml,json}` where `RUN_MODE=$APP_ENV` (optional)\n    ///  3. Environment variables (`APP__POSTGRES__HOST=\u2026`)\n    ///\n    /// The merge strategy is \u201clast one wins\u201d.\n    pub fn load() -> Result<Self, ConfigLoadError> {\n        let env = std::env::var(\"APP_ENV\").unwrap_or_else(|_| \"local\".into());\n        let mut cfg = Config::builder();\n\n        // tier 1\n        cfg = cfg.add_source(File::with_name(\"config/default\").required(false));\n\n        // tier 2\n        cfg = cfg.add_source(File::with_name(&format!(\"config/{}\", env)).required(false));\n\n        // tier 3 (env vars). Double underscore `__` = nesting delimiter.\n        cfg = cfg.add_source(\n            Environment::with_prefix(\"APP\")\n                .separator(\"__\")\n                .list_separator(\",\"),\n        );\n\n        // finish\n        cfg.build()\n            .map_err(ConfigLoadError::Parse)?\n            .try_deserialize::<AppConfig>()\n            .map_err(ConfigLoadError::Deserialize)\n    }\n}\n\n/// Errors that might occur while loading the configuration.\n#[derive(Debug, Error)]\npub enum ConfigLoadError {\n    #[error(\"config file parsing failed: {0}\")]\n    Parse(ConfigError),\n    #[error(\"config deserialization failed: {0}\")]\n    Deserialize(ConfigError),\n}\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n/*                               Sub-structures                               */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)]\npub struct HttpConfig {\n    #[serde(default = \"default_bind_addr\")]\n    pub bind: IpAddr,\n    #[serde(default = \"default_port\")]\n    pub port: u16,\n    #[serde(default = \"default_request_timeout_secs\")]\n    pub request_timeout: Duration,\n    #[serde(default)]\n    pub enable_graphql_playground: bool,\n}\n\nfn default_bind_addr() -> IpAddr {\n    IpAddr::from([0, 0, 0, 0])\n}\nfn default_port() -> u16 {\n    8080\n}\nfn default_request_timeout_secs() -> Duration {\n    Duration::from_secs(30)\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)]\npub struct PostgresConfig {\n    pub host: String,\n    #[serde(default = \"default_pg_port\")]\n    pub port: u16,\n    pub dbname: String,\n    pub username: String,\n    #[serde(deserialize_with = \"deser_secret\")]\n    pub password: SecretString,\n    #[serde(default = \"default_pg_pool_size\")]\n    pub max_pool_size: u32,\n    #[serde(default)]\n    pub require_ssl: bool,\n}\n\nfn default_pg_port() -> u16 {\n    5432\n}\nfn default_pg_pool_size() -> u32 {\n    20\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)]\npub struct RedisConfig {\n    pub url: String,\n    #[serde(default = \"default_redis_pool_size\")]\n    pub pool_size: u32,\n    #[serde(default)]\n    pub cache_ttl: Option<humantime::Duration>,\n}\n\nfn default_redis_pool_size() -> u32 {\n    16\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)]\npub struct AuthConfig {\n    pub jwt_issuer: String,\n    pub jwks_endpoint: String,\n    #[serde(deserialize_with = \"deser_secret\")]\n    pub api_key: SecretString,\n    #[serde(default = \"default_token_ttl\")]\n    pub token_ttl: Duration,\n}\n\nfn default_token_ttl() -> Duration {\n    Duration::from_secs(60 * 60) // 1 hour\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)]\npub struct PaginationConfig {\n    #[serde(default = \"default_page_size\")]\n    pub default_page_size: u32,\n    #[serde(default = \"default_max_page_size\")]\n    pub max_page_size: u32,\n}\n\nfn default_page_size() -> u32 {\n    50\n}\nfn default_max_page_size() -> u32 {\n    200\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)]\npub struct ResponseCacheConfig {\n    #[serde(default)]\n    pub enabled: bool,\n    #[serde(default = \"default_cache_duration\")]\n    pub duration: Duration,\n    #[serde(default)]\n    pub respect_cache_control_header: bool,\n}\n\nfn default_cache_duration() -> Duration {\n    Duration::from_secs(5 * 60) // 5 minutes\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)]\npub struct LoggingConfig {\n    #[serde(default = \"default_log_level\")]\n    pub level: LogLevel,\n    #[serde(default)]\n    pub json: bool,\n}\n\nfn default_log_level() -> LogLevel {\n    LogLevel::Info\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)]\n#[serde(rename_all = \"lowercase\")]\npub enum LogLevel {\n    Trace,\n    Debug,\n    Info,\n    Warn,\n    Error,\n}\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n/*                     Helpers / bespoke deserialization logic                */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n/// Custom `serde` helper to ensure secrets are never leaked via `Debug`.\nfn deser_secret<'de, D>(deserializer: D) -> Result<SecretString, D::Error>\nwhere\n    D: serde::Deserializer<'de>,\n{\n    let s: String = String::deserialize(deserializer)?;\n    Ok(SecretString::new(s))\n}\n\n/// Output a PostgreSQL connection string (excluding password) for telemetry.\n/// NOTE: the password is intentionally omitted to avoid traces leaking secrets.\nimpl PostgresConfig {\n    pub fn safe_dsn(&self) -> String {\n        format!(\n            \"host={} port={} user={} dbname={} sslmode={}\",\n            self.host,\n            self.port,\n            self.username,\n            self.dbname,\n            if cfg.postgres.password.expose_secret(),\n            \"sekret\",\n            \"env secret should override\"\n        );\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn default_values_are_applied() {\n        let cfg = timeout(Duration::from_millis(30), conn.get(key)).await??;\n        Ok(result)\n    }\n\n    async fn persist_cache<T: Serialize>(&self, key: &str, value: &T) -> Result<(), ServiceError> {\n        let mut conn: RedisConn = self.redis.get().await?;\n        let data = serde_json::to_vec(value)?;\n        let _: () = conn\n            .set_ex(key, data, 60) // 60 seconds TTL\n            .await\n            .map_err(ServiceError::Cache)?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Error)]\npub enum ServiceError {\n    #[error(\"repository error: {0}\")]\n    Repo(#[from] It demonstrates the project\u2019s MVVM-inspired layering:\n//!\n//! Dependencies (Cargo.toml excerpt):\n//! ----------------------------------\n//! [dependencies]\n//! actix-web       = \"4\"\n//! actix-web-httpauth = \"0.7\"\n//! serde           = { version = \"1\", features = [\"derive\"] }\n//! serde_json      = \"1\"\n//! validator       = \"0.16\"\n//! uuid            = { version = \"1\", features = [\"v4\", \"serde\", \"macro-diagnostics\"] }\n//! chrono          = { version = \"0.4\", features = [\"serde\"] }\n//! redis           = { version = \"0.23\", features = [\"tokio-comp\"] }\n//! async-trait     = \"0.1\"\n//! tracing         = \"0.1\"\n//! thiserror       = \"1\"\n//! futures         = \"0.3\"\n//! parking_lot     = \"0.12\"\n//!\n//! -------------------------------------------------------------\n//! Option<DateTime<Utc>>,\n\n    /// Optional sorting hint \u2013 \"asc\"|\"desc\"  (default: \"desc\")\n    #[serde(default = \"default_sort\")]\n    #[validate(custom = \"validate_sort\")]\n    pub parameter\nfn validate_sort(sort: &str) -> Result<(), ValidationError> {\n    match sort {\n        \"asc\" | \"desc\" => Ok(()),\n        _ => Err(ValidationError::new(\"invalid_sort\")),\n    }\n}\n\n/// --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n/// Domain Model (read-side projection, a subset of the full LedgerEntry aggregate)\n/// --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n#[derive(Debug, Serialize, Clone)]\npub struct LedgerEntry {\n    pub id: Uuid,\n    pub account_id: Uuid,\n    pub amount_minor: i64,\n    pub currency: String,\n    pub booked_at: DateTime<Utc>,\n    pub narrative: String,\n}\n\n/// --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n/// Pagination envelope returned to clients\n/// --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n#[derive(Debug, Serialize)]\npub struct Paginated<T> {\n    pub data: Vec<T>,\n    pub page: usize,\n    pub per_page: usize,\n    pub total: usize,\n}\n\n/// --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n/// Cache key utilities\n/// --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\nfn make_cache_key(user_tenant: &str, dto: &LedgerEntryQueryDto) -> String {\n    // A simple but effective .map(Uuid::to_string)\n            .unwrap_or_else(|| \"all\".into()),\n        dto.from_date\n            .map(|d| d.timestamp_millis().to_string())\n            .unwrap_or_else(|| \"min\".into()),\n        dto.to_date\n            .map(|d| d.timestamp_millis().to_string())\n            .unwrap_or_else(|| \"max\".into()),\n        dto.sort\n    )\n}\n\n///   ApiError::Internal(_) => StatusCode::INTERNAL_SERVER_ERROR,\n        }\n    }\n\n    fn error_response(&self) -> HttpResponse {\n        // Structured error envelope\n        #[derive(Serialize)]\n LedgerEntry,\n            r#\"\n            SELECT id, tenant_id, account_id, amount, currency, booked_at, memo\n            FROM   ledger_entries\n            WHERE  tenant_id = $1 AND id = $2\n #[instrument(skip(self), level = \"debug\")]\n    async fn fetch_page(\n        &self,\n        tenant_id: i64,\n        req: PageRequest,\n    ) -> Result<(Vec<LedgerEntry>, u64)> {\n        // 1. Count total for the tenant.\n        let total: (i64,) = sqlx::query_as(\n            r#\"SELECT COUNT(*) as count FROM ledger_entries WHERE tenant_id = $1\"#,\n        )\n        .bind(tenant_id)\n        .fetch_one(&self.pool)\n        .await?;\n\n        // 2. Fetch requested slice.\n        let rows = sqlx::query_as!(\n            LedgerEntry,\n            r#\"\n            SELECT id, tenant_id, account_id, amount, currency, booked_at, memo\n            FROM   ledger_entries\n            WHERE  tenant_id = $1\n            ORDER  BY booked_at DESC, id DESC\n            OFFSET $2 LIMIT $3\n        \"#,\n            tenant_id,\n            req.offset(),\n            req.per_page as i64\n        )\n        .fetch_all(&self.pool)\n        .await?;\n\n        Ok((rows, total.0 as u64))\n    }\n}\n\n/// High-level service orchestrating repository and distributed cache.\n///\n/// Caches individual `LedgerEntryDto` objects to minimise DB traffic for\n/// idempotent GET requests. The caching strategy is a simple \u201ccache-aside\u201d\n/// with a 10 minute TTL. We purposely keep the implementation thin; in real\n/// life we would centralise this logic through a reusable Redis wrapper.\n#[derive(Clone)]\npub struct LedgerEntryService<R: LedgerEntryRepository> {\n    repo: Arc<R>,\n    redis: redis::Client,\n    // Small in-memory cache to ameliorate thundering herd during short periods.\n    in_memory: Arc<RwLock<lru::LruCache<i64, LedgerEntryDto>>>,\n}\n\nimpl<R: LedgerEntryRepository> LedgerEntryService<R> {\n    pub fn new(repo: R, redis_url: &str, mem_cache_cap: usize) -> Result<Self> {\n        Ok(Self {\n            repo: Arc::new(repo),\n            redis: redis::Client::open(redis_url).map_err(LedgerError::Cache)?,\n            in_memory: Arc::new(RwLock::new(lru::LruCache::new(\n                mem_cache_cap.try_into().unwrap_or(256),\n            ))),\n        })\n    }\n\n    fn redis_key(tenant_id: i64, entry_id: i64) -> String {\n        format!(\"tenant:{tenant_id}:ledger_entry:{entry_id}\")\n    }\n\n    /// Inserts a new entry and invalidates affected caches.\n    #[instrument(skip(self, entry), level = \"info\")]\n    pub async fn create_entry(&self, entry: &LedgerEntry) -> Result<i64> {\n        // Basic validation rule: amount cannot be 0.\n        if entry.amount.is_zero() {\n            return Err(LedgerError::InvalidState(\n                \"Amount cannot be zero\".to_string(),\n            ));\n        }\n\n        let id = self.repo.insert(entry).await?;\n\n        // Invalidate parent list (simple strategy: delete entire key space).\n        let mut conn = self.redis.get_async_connection().await?;\n        let pattern = format!(\"tenant:{}:ledger_entry:*\", entry.tenant_id);\n        let _: () = redis::cmd(\"UNLINK\").arg(pattern).query_async(&mut conn).await?;\n\n        // Evict in-memory cache.\n        self.in_memory.write().await.pop(&id);\n\n        Ok(id)\n    }\n\n    /// Fetches a single entry, going through L1 (memory) & L2 (Redis) caches.\n    #[instrument(skip(self), level = \"debug\")]\n    pub async fn get_entry(\n        &self,\n        tenant_id: i64,\n        entry_id: i64,\n    ) -> Result<LedgerEntryDto> {\n        // 1. Check L1.\n        if let Some(dto) = self.in_memory.read().await.get(&entry_id).cloned() {\n            return Ok(dto);\n        }\n\n        // 2. Check Redis.\n        let redis_key = Self::redis_key(tenant_id, entry_id);\n        let mut conn = self.redis.get_async_connection().await?;\n        if let Ok(Some(binary)) = conn.get::<_, Vec<u8>>(&redis_key).await {\n            let dto: LedgerEntryDto = bincode::deserialize(&binary)\n                .map_err(|e| LedgerError::InvalidState(e.to_string()))?;\n            // Fill L1.\n            self.in_memory.write().await.put(entry_id, dto.clone());\n            return Ok(dto);\n        }\n\n        // 3. Fallback to DB.\n        let entry = self.repo.get(tenant_id, entry_id).await?;\n        let dto = LedgerEntryDto::from(entry.clone());\n\n        // Back-fill caches.\n        let _: () = conn\n            .set_ex(\n                &redis_key,\n                bincode::serialize(&dto).unwrap(),\n                600, // seconds\n            )\n            .await?;\n        self.in_memory.write().await.put(entry_id, dto.clone());\n\n        Ok(dto)\n    }\n\n    /// Retrieves a paginated list, with optional total count.\n    #[instrument(skip(self), level = \"debug\")]\n    pub async fn list_entries(\n        &self,\n        tenant_id: i64,\n        req: PageRequest,\n    ) -> Result<Page<LedgerEntryDto>> {\n        let req = req.sanitise();\n        // At scale we would paginated-cache \u201cpages\u201d too, but omit for brevity.\n        let (rows, total) = self.repo.fetch_page(tenant_id, req).await?;\n        let data: Vec<LedgerEntryDto> = rows.into_iter().map(Into::into).collect();\n\n        let consumed = (req.page as u64) * (req.per_page as u64);\n        let next_page = if consumed < total {\n            Some(req.page + 1)\n        } else {\n            None\n        };\n\n        Ok(Page {\n            data,\n            next_page,\n            total: Some(total),\n        })\n    }\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n    use rust_decimal_macros::dec;\n    use serial_test::serial;\n\n    // Helper to build an in-memory postgres (requires `cargo test -- --ignored`\n    // if dockerised). Kept minimal for brevity.\n    async fn bootstrap_repo() -> PostgresLedgerEntryRepo {\n        let db_url =\n            std::env::var(\"TEST_DATABASE_URL\").expect(\"Set TEST_DATABASE_URL\");\n        let repo = PostgresLedgerEntryRepo::new(&db_url, 5)\n            .await\n            .expect(\"failed to init repo\");\n\n        // Initialise schema (idempotent).\n        sqlx::migrate!().run(&repo.pool).await.unwrap();\n\n        repo\n    }\n\n    #[tokio::test]\n    #[serial] // Avoid test inter-dependency on the DB.\n    async fn crud_roundtrip() {\n        let repo = bootstrap_repo().await;\n        let svc =\n            LedgerEntryService::new(repo, \"redis://127.0.0.1/\", 128).unwrap();\n\n        let entry = LedgerEntry {\n            id: 0,\n            tenant_id: 42,\n            account_id: 100,\n            amount: dec!(123.45),\n            currency: \"USD\".into(),\n            booked_at: Utc::now(),\n            memo: Some(\"integration test\".into()),\n        };\n\n        let id = svc.create_entry(&entry).await.unwrap();\n        assert!(id > 0);\n\n        let dto1 = svc.get_entry(42, id).await.unwrap();\n        let dto2 = svc.get_entry(42, id).await.unwrap(); // should hit cache\n\n        assert_eq!(dto1.amount, dto2.amount);\n\n        let page = svc\n            .list_entries(\n                42,\n                PageRequest {\n                    page: 1,\n                    per_page: 10,\n                },\n            )\n            .await\n            .unwrap();\n        assert_eq!(page.data.len(), 1);\n    }\n}\n```",

vec![Box::new(filter.tenant_id)];\n\n        if let Some(from) = filter.booked_from {\n            conditions.push(format!(\"booked_date >= ${}\", binds.len() + 1));\n            binds.push(Box::new(from));\n        }\n        if let Some(to) = filter.booked_to {\n            conditions.push(format!(\"booked_date <= ${}\", binds.len() + 1));\n            binds.push(Box::new(to));\n        }\n        if let Some(ref prefix) = filter.account_prefix {\n            conditions.push(format!(\"account_code LIKE ${}\", binds.len() + 1));\n            binds.push(Box::new(format!(\"{}%\", prefix)));\n        }\n\n        let where_clause = conditions.iter().join(\" AND \");\n\n        // total count\n        let count_query = format!(\"SELECT COUNT(*) FROM ledger_entries WHERE {}\", where_clause);\n        let total: i64 = sqlx::query_scalar_with(&count_query, binds.iter().map(|b| &**b))\n            .fetch_one(&self.pool)\n            .await\n            .map_err(LedgerError::Database)?;\n\n        // data query\n        let offset = (pagination.page - 1) * pagination.per_page;\n        let mut data_query = format!(\n            \"SELECT * FROM ledger_entries WHERE {} ORDER BY booked_date DESC, id DESC LIMIT {} OFFSET {}\",\n            where_clause, pagination.per_page, offset\n        );\n        // We cannot use binds for LIMIT/OFFSET easily with sqlx::query! macro; safe as numbers.\n\n        let rows = sqlx::query(&data_query)\n            .bind_all(binds) // extension, see below\n            .fetch_all(&self.pool)\n            .await\n            .map_err(LedgerError::Database)?;\n\n        let entries = rows\n            .into_iter()\n            .map(|row| LedgerEntry {\n                id: row.get(\"id\"),\n                tenant_id: row.get(\"tenant_id\"),\n                booked_date: row.get(\"booked_date\"),\n                account_code: row.get(\"account_code\"),\n                currency: row.get(\"currency\"),\n                debit: row.get(\"debit\"),\n                credit: row.get(\"credit\"),\n                narrative: row.get(\"narrative\"),\n                created_at: row.get(\"created_at\"),\n                updated_at: row.get(\"updated_at\"),\n            })\n            .collect();\n\n        Ok((entries, total as u64))\n    }\n}\n\n/* ---------------------------------------------------------------- *\\\n * Caching\n\\* ---------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n/// A very small subset of the redis crate API to keep the snippet\u2019s dependency\n/// tree lean. In production, replace with `redis::aio::ConnectionLike` et al.\n#[async_trait]\npub trait Cache: Send + Sync {\n    async fn get_bytes(&self, key: &str) -> Result<Option<Vec<u8>>, LedgerError>;\n    async fn set_bytes(&self, key: &str, value: &[u8], ttl: Duration) -> Result<(), LedgerError>;\n}\n\n/// Redis implementation.\npub struct RedisCache {\n    client: redis::Client,\n}\n\nimpl RedisCache {\n    pub fn new(connection_string: &str) -> Result<Self, LedgerError> {\n        let client =\n            redis::Client::open(connection_string).map_err(|e| LedgerError::cache(e.to_string()))?;\n        Ok(Self { client })\n    }\n\n    async fn conn(&self) -> Result<redis::aio::Connection, LedgerError> {\n        self.client\n            .get_async_connection()\n            .await\n            .map_err(|e| LedgerError::cache(e.to_string()))\n    }\n}\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl Cache for RedisCache {\n    async fn get_bytes(&self, key: &str) -> Result<Option<Vec<u8>>, LedgerError> {\n        let mut conn = self.conn().await?;\n        let bytes: Option<Vec<u8>> =\n            redis::cmd(\"GET\").arg(key).query_async(&mut conn).await.map_err(|e| LedgerError::cache(e.to_string()))?;\n        Ok(bytes)\n    }\n\n    async fn set_bytes(&self, key: &str, value: &[u8], ttl: Duration) -> Result<(), LedgerError> {\n        let mut conn = self.conn().await?;\n        redis::cmd(\"SET\")\n            .arg(key)\n            .arg(value)\n            .arg(\"PX\")\n            .arg(ttl.as_millis() as u64)\n            .query_async(&mut conn)\n            .await\n            .map_err(|e| LedgerError::cache(e.to_string()))?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/* ---------------------------------------------------------------- *\\\n * Service Layer\n\\* ---------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n#[derive(Clone)]\npub struct LedgerEntryQueryService<R: LedgerEntryRepository, C: Cache> {\n    repository: Arc<R>,\n    cache: Arc<C>,\n}\n\nimpl<R: LedgerEntryRepository, C: Cache> LedgerEntryQueryService<R, C> {\n    pub fn new(repository: Arc<R>, cache: Arc<C>) -> Self {\n        Self { repository, cache }\n    }\n\n    /// High-level query function to be consumed by HTTP/GraphQL handlers.\n    pub async fn list_entries(\n        &self,\n        filter: LedgerEntryFilter,\n        pagination: Pagination,\n    ) -> Result<LedgerEntryPage, LedgerError> {\n        // Step 1: validate user input\n        filter.validate()?;\n        pagination.validate()?;\n\n        // Step 2: cache lookup\n        let cache_key = Self::make_cache_key(&filter, &pagination);\n        if let Some(bytes) = self.cache.get_bytes(&cache_key).await? {\n            let page: LedgerEntryPage = serde_json::from_slice(&bytes)?;\n            return Ok(page);\n        }\n\n        // Step 3: fetch from repository\n        let (items, total_items) = self.repository.fetch_entries(&filter, &pagination).await?;\n        let total_pages = ((total_items as f64) / (pagination.per_page as f64)).ceil() as u32;\n\n        let page = LedgerEntryPage {\n            items,\n            total_items,\n            total_pages,\n            page: pagination.page,\n            per_page: pagination.per_page,\n            cache_ttl_secs: CACHE_TTL.as_secs(),\n        };\n\n        // Step 4: store in cache (best-effort)\n        if let Ok(bytes) = serde_json::to_vec(&page) {\n            let _ = self\n                .cache\n                .set_bytes(&cache_key, &bytes, CACHE_TTL)\n                .await;\n        }\n\n        Ok(page)\n    }\n\n    fn make_cache_key(filter: &LedgerEntryFilter, pagination: &Pagination) -> String {\n        let raw_key = serde_json::to_string(&(filter, pagination)).unwrap_or_default();\n        let digest = Sha256::digest(raw_key.as_bytes());\n        format!(\"ledger_entries:{:x}\", digest)\n    }\n}\n\n/* ---------------------------------------------------------------- *\\\n * \u2014\u2014\u2014 Helper extension for dynamic binds (prepared at runtime) \u2014\u2014\u2014\n\\* ---------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n/// Trait to attach a dynamic iterator of boxed Send + Sync)>;\n}\n\nimpl<'q> QueryBindAll<'q> for sqlx::query::Query<'q, Postgres, sqlx::postgres::PgArguments> {\n    fn bind_all<I>(mut self, binds: I) -> Self\n    where\n        I: IntoIterator<Item = &'q (dyn sqlx::Encode<'q, Postgres> + sqlx::Type<Postgres> + Send + Sync)>,\n    {\n        for b in binds {\n            self = self.bind(b);\n        }\n        self\n    }\n}\n\n/* ---------------------------------------------------------------- *\\\n * \u27e6 Tests \u27e7 \u2014 can be run with `cargo test -p api_microservice`\n\\* #[tokio::test]\n    async fn test_validation_fails_for_bad_pagination() {\n        let service = LedgerEntryQueryService::new(\n            Arc::new(MockRepo),\n validate_offset(offset: &u32) -> Result<(), ValidationError> {\n    if *offset > 100_000 {\n        return Err(ValidationError::new(\"offset_too_large\"));\n    }\n    Ok(())\n}\n\n/// Custom limit Err(ValidationError::new(\"limit_out_of_bounds\"));\n    }\n    Ok(())\n}\n\nimpl Pagination {\n    /// Tries to build a [`Pagination`] struct from an arbitrary query map,\n    /// returning .get(\"offset\")\n            .and_then(|v| v.parse::<u32>().ok())\n            .unwrap_or_default();\n\n        let limit = params\n            .get(\"limit\")\n            .and_then(|v| candidate.validate()?;\n\n        Ok(candidate)\n    }\n\n    /// Calculates SQL LIMIT/OFFSET for the current page.\n    #[must_use]\n    pub fn sql_limit_offset(&self) -> (u32, u32) {\n        (self.limit, self.offset)\n    }\n}\n\n/// The envelope returned by list-style endpoints.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize)]\npub struct Paginated<T>\nwhere\n    T: Serialize,\n{\n    pub items:       Vec<T>,\n    pub total:       u64,\n    pub offset:      u32,\n    pub limit:       u32,\n    pub has_more:    bool,\n    #[serde(skip_serializing_if = \"Option::is_none\")]\n    pub cache_hint:  ) -> Self {\n        let has_more = (pagination.offset as u64 + items.len() as u64) < total;\n        let cache_hint = cacheable.then(|| CacheHint::new(DEFAULT_TTL_SECONDS));\n\n        Self {\n }\n}\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl PaginatedRepository for LedgerEntryPgRepository {\n    type Output = LedgerEntry;\n\n    #[instrument(skip_all, name = \"repo.ledger.list\")]\n    async fn       \"amount:asc\"      => builder.push(\"ORDER BY amount ASC \"),\n                \"amount:desc\"     => builder.push(\"ORDER BY amount DESC \"),\n                _ => {\n This module deliberately focuses on the\n//! \u201cQuery\u201d half of CQRS, while remaining agnostic of the web framework that\n//! ultimately wires it up to REST/GraphQL routes.\n//!\n//! # Overview\n//!\n//! \u2022 `LedgerEntry`: Domain Model  \n//! \u2022 `LedgerEntryView`: DTO for external representation  \n//! \u2022 `Pagination`: Helper for page/size bounds + validation  \n//! String, // e.g., `\"123.45 USD\"`\n    pub direction:    EntryType,\n    pub created_at:   DateTime<Utc>,\n    pub description:  Option<String>,\n}\n\nimpl From<LedgerEntry> for LedgerEntryView {\n    fn from(src: LedgerEntry) -> Self {\n        let sign = if src.entry_type == EntryType::Debit { \"-\" } else { \"\" };\n        // Assume 2 decimal places for simplicity; a production system would\n        // leverage `rust_decimal` or similar.\n        let amount_major = (src.amount_minor as f64) / 100.0;\n        LedgerEntryView {\n            id:          src.id,\n            account_id:         return Err(LedgerError::validation(&format!(\n                \"`per_page` must be in 1..={MAX_PER_PAGE}\"\n            )));\n        }\n        Ok(Self { page, per_page })\n    }\n\n    pub fn offset_limit(self) -> (i64, i64) {\n        (\n            ((self.page - 1) * self.per_page) as i64,\n            self.per_page as i64,\n        )\n    }\n}\n\n/// Server response envelope for paginated lists.\n#[derive(Debug, Serialize)]\npub struct Paginated<T> {\n    pub data:       Vec<T>,\n    pub total:      u64,\n    pub page:       u32,\n    pub per_page:   u32,\n}\n\n// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n// Errors\n// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n/// Domain-level error type.\n#[derive(Debug, Error)]\npub enum LedgerError {\n    #[error(\"Validation error: {0}\")]\n    Validation(String),\n\n    #[error(\"Database error: {0}\")]\n    Database(#[from] sqlx::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"Cache error: {0}\")]\n    Cache(#[from] deadpool_redis::redis::RedisError),\n\n    #[error(\"Internal error: {0}\")]\n    Internal(String),\n}\n\nimpl LedgerError {\n    fn validation(msg: &str) -> Self { Self::Validation(msg.to_owned()) }\n}\n\nimpl actix_web::ResponseError for LedgerError {} // Optional integration\n\n// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n// Repository Trait\n// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n#[async_trait]\npub trait LedgerEntryRepository: Send + Sync + fmt::Debug {\n    /// Return (entries, total) for a given account with pagination.\n    async fn fetch_by_account(\n        &self,\n        account_id: Uuid,\n        pagination: Pagination,\n    ) -> Result<(Vec<LedgerEntry>, u64), LedgerError>;\n}\n\n// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n// Repository Implementation (PostgreSQL)\n// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n#[derive(Debug)]\npub struct PostgresLedgerEntryRepository {\n    pool: PgPool,\n}\n\nimpl PostgresLedgerEntryRepository {\n    pub fn new(pool: PgPool) -> Self { Self { pool } }\n}\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl LedgerEntryRepository for PostgresLedgerEntryRepository {\n    #[instrument(skip(self))]\n    async fn fetch_by_account(\n        &self,\n        account_id: Uuid,\n        pagination: Pagination,\n    ) -> Result<(Vec<LedgerEntry>, u64), LedgerError> {\n        let (offset, limit) = pagination.offset_limit();\n\n        let mut tx = self.pool.begin().await?;\n\n        let entries: Vec<LedgerEntry> = sqlx::query!(\n            r#\"\n            SELECT id, account_id, amount_minor, currency, entry_type as \"entry_type: EntryType\",\n                   created_at, description\n              FROM ledger_entries\n             WHERE account_id = $1\n             ORDER BY created_at DESC\n             OFFSET $2 LIMIT $3\n            \"#,\n            account_id,\n            offset,\n            limit\n        )\n        .map(|row| LedgerEntry {\n            id:           row.id,\n            account_id:   row.account_id,\n            amount_minor: row.amount_minor,\n            currency:     row.currency,\n            entry_type:   row.entry_type,\n            created_at:   row.created_at,\n            description:  row.description,\n        })\n        .fetch_all(&mut *tx)\n        .await?;\n\n        // Total rows\n        let total: i64 = sqlx::query_scalar!(\n            r#\"SELECT COUNT(*) FROM ledger_entries WHERE account_id = $1\"#,\n            account_id\n        )\n        .fetch_one(&mut *tx)\n        .await?;\n\n        tx.commit().await?;\n\n        Ok((entries, total as u64))\n    }\n}\n\n// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n// Service Layer\n// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\nconst CACHE_TTL: Duration = Duration::from_secs(60); // 1-minute soft TTL\n\n#[derive(Clone)]\npub struct LedgerQueryService {\n    repo:      Arc<dyn LedgerEntryRepository>,\n    cache:     RedisPool,\n}\n\nimpl LedgerQueryService {\n    pub fn new<R>(repo: R, cache: RedisPool) -> Self\n    where\n        R: LedgerEntryRepository + 'static,\n    {\n        Self {\n            repo: Arc::new(repo),\n            cache,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Fetch paginated ledger entries with Redis caching.\n    ///\n    /// Cache key is constructed from `account_id/page/per_page`.\n    #[instrument(skip(self))]\n    pub async fn list_entries(\n        &self,\n        account_id: Uuid,\n        pagination: Pagination,\n    ) -> Result<Paginated<LedgerEntryView>, LedgerError> {\n        let cache_key = format!(\n            \"ledger:v1:entries:{}:{}:{}\",\n            account_id, pagination.page, pagination.per_page\n        );\n\n        // Step 1. Try cache\n        let mut redis_con = self.cache.get().await?;\n        if let Ok(Some(cached_json)) = redis_con.get::<_, String>(&cache_key).await {\n            debug!(%cache_key, \"Cache hit for ledger entries\");\n            let paginated: Paginated<LedgerEntryView> = serde_json::from_str(&cached_json)\n                .map_err(|e| LedgerError::Internal(e.to_string()))?;\n            return Ok(paginated);\n        }\n        debug!(%cache_key, \"Cache miss for ledger entries\");\n\n        // Step 2. Query repository\n        let (entries, total) = self.repo.fetch_by_account(account_id, pagination).await?;\n\n        let data: Vec<_> = entries.into_iter().map(LedgerEntryView::from).collect();\n\n        let result = Paginated {\n            data:     data.clone(),\n            total,\n            page:     pagination.page,\n            per_page: pagination.per_page,\n        };\n\n        // Step 3. Fire-and-forget cache population\n        let cache_payload = serde_json::to_string(&result)\n            .map_err(|e| LedgerError::Internal(e.to_string()))?;\n        let mut redis_con_clone = redis_con.clone();\n        tokio::spawn(async move {\n            let _: Result<(), _> = redis_con_clone\n                .set_ex::<_, _, ()>(&cache_key, cache_payload, CACHE_TTL.as_secs() as usize)\n                .await;\n        });\n\n        Ok(result)\n    }\n}\n\n// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n// Unit Tests\n// Contains an in-process read/write lock guard around the\n/// connection to avoid stampeding\u2010herd scenarios in high load.\n#[derive(Clone)]\npub struct ResponseCache {\n    conn: Arc<RwLock<ConnectionManager>>,\n    prefix: String,\n}\n\nimpl ResponseCache {\n    /// Create a new instance from an existing Redis connection.\n    pub fn new(prefix: impl Into<String>, conn: ConnectionManager) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            conn: Arc::new(RwLock::new(conn)),\n            prefix: prefix.into(),\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Assemble a namespaced key for Redis. Miss \u2192 resolve & fill cache\n        let resolved = query.resolve().await?;\n        self.write(&ns, &key, &resolved, query.policy()).await?;\n\n        Ok(resolved)\n    }\n\n    /// Remove all keys for a given tenant namespace.  Useful when a ledger\n    /// mutation happens and cached projections must be invalidated.\n    #[instrument(skip(self))]\n    pub async fn purge_namespace(&self, namespace: &str) -> Result<u64, here.\n        let keys: Vec<String> = conn.keys(pattern).await?;\n        let deleted: u64 = conn.del(keys).await?;\n        debug!(\"purged {} stale cache entries under '{}'\", deleted,   "content": "# Solution: rust_api_microservice_expert_008_architectural_understanding_expert_01\n\n## Key Files Identified\n\n### Caching Modules\n- `/app/project/src/module_9.txt` - Core response cache layer with `ResponseCache::purge_namespace()` invalidation method\n- `/app/project/src/module_44.txt` - Ledger Entry listing with Redis response-level caching (read handler)\n- `/app/project/src/module_72.txt` - Pagination + Response Caching facade with `purge()` method\n\n### Read Handler Modules (GET Operations)\n- `/app/project/src/module_26.txt` - Ledger Entry Query Endpoint using actix-web with `#[get(\"/api/v1/ledger/entries\")]` route\n- `/app/project/src/module_52.txt` - High-frequency paginated read-model with Redis response-caching via `LedgerEntryService`\n- `/app/project/src/module_44.txt` - Ledger Entry listing via `list_ledger_entries_handler` with Axum\n\n### Write Handler Modules (INSERT/UPDATE Operations)\n- `/app/project/src/module_38.txt` - Contains `insert()` method that writes to DB without cache invalidation\n- `/app/project/src/module_67.txt` - `LedgerEntryService::create_entry()` with partial cache invalidation (only individual entry cache, not paginated response cache)\n\n### Configuration\n- `/app/project/src/config.txt` - Contains `ResponseCacheConfig` with `duration` (default 5 minutes TTL) and `enabled` flag\n\n## Code Evidence\n\n### Core Caching Module with Invalidation Support (module_9.txt)\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/module_9.txt\n// Lines: 185-196\n\n    /// Remove all keys for a given tenant namespace.  Useful when a ledger\n    /// mutation happens and cached projections must be invalidated.\n    #[instrument(skip(self))]\n    pub async fn purge_namespace(&self, namespace: &str) -> Result<u64, CacheError> {\n        let pattern = format!(\"{}:{}:*\", self.prefix, namespace);\n        let mut conn = self.conn.write().await;\n        // NOTE: SCAN could be more graceful for prod, kept simple here.\n        let keys: Vec<String> = conn.keys(pattern).await?;\n        let deleted: u64 = conn.del(keys).await?;\n        debug!(\"purged {} stale cache entries under '{}'\", deleted, namespace);\n        Ok(deleted)\n    }\n```\n\n### Read Handler with Caching (module_44.txt)\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/module_44.txt\n// Lines: 355-408\n\n    #[instrument(skip(self))]\n    pub async fn list(\n        &self,\n        tenant: Uuid,\n        query: ListQuery,\n    ) -> Result<Paginated<LedgerEntryDto>, ServiceError> {\n        // 1. Try cache (30ms timeout to avoid head-of-line blocking)\n        let key = Self::cache_key(tenant, &query);\n        if let Ok(Some(raw)) = self.try_fetch_cache(&key).await {\n            debug!(%tenant, %key, \"Cache hit\");\n            return serde_json::from_slice::<Paginated<LedgerEntryDto>>(&raw)\n                .map_err(ServiceError::CacheSerialization);\n        }\n\n        // 2. Query repository\n        debug!(%tenant, \"Cache miss \u2013 querying DB\");\n        let (entries, total) = self.repo.list(tenant, &query).await?;\n        // ... builds paginated response ...\n\n        // 3. Backfill cache (best-effort)\n        let _ = self.persist_cache(&key, &payload).await;\n\n        Ok(payload)\n    }\n\n    async fn persist_cache<T: Serialize>(&self, key: &str, value: &T) -> Result<(), ServiceError> {\n        let mut conn: RedisConn = self.redis.get().await?;\n        let data = serde_json::to_vec(value)?;\n        let _: () = conn\n            .set_ex(key, data, 60) // 60 seconds TTL\n            .await\n            .map_err(ServiceError::Cache)?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n```\n\n### Write Handler WITHOUT Cache Invalidation (module_38.txt)\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/module_38.txt\n// Lines: 282-306\n\n/// An *idempotent* command that inserts a ledger entry inside its own\n/// transaction.  Exposed as a convenience; not part of the trait.\n///\n/// Demonstrates how we keep read & write paths separated (`CQRS` style).\nimpl LedgerEntryPgRepository {\n    #[instrument(skip_all, name = \"repo.ledger.insert\")]\n    pub async fn insert(&self, entry: &LedgerEntry) -> Result<(), PaginationError> {\n        let mut tx = self.pool.begin().await?;\n\n        sqlx::query(\n            r#\"\n            INSERT INTO ledger_entries\n            (id, account_id, amount, currency, description, created_at)\n            VALUES ($1, $2, $3, $4, $5, $6)\n            ON CONFLICT (id) DO NOTHING\n            \"#,\n        )\n        .bind(entry.id)\n        .bind(entry.account_id)\n        .bind(entry.amount)\n        .bind(&entry.currency)\n        .bind(&entry.description)\n        .bind(entry.created_at)\n        .execute(&mut tx)\n        .await?;\n\n        tx.commit().await?;\n        Ok(())\n        // NOTE: NO CACHE INVALIDATION IS PERFORMED HERE\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Read Handler with Response Caching (module_26.txt)\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/module_26.txt\n// Lines: 317-386\n\n#[get(\"/api/v1/ledger/entries\")]\n#[instrument(skip(dto, state, auth), fields(tenant = %auth.tenant_id))]\npub async fn get_ledger_entries(\n    auth: AuthContext,\n    Query(dto): Query<LedgerEntryQueryDto>,\n    state: Data<AppState>,\n) -> Result<Json<Paginated<LedgerEntry>>, ApiError> {\n    // ... validation ...\n\n    let cache_key = make_cache_key(&auth.tenant_id, &dto);\n\n    // Attempt cache hit\n    if let Ok(cached) = redis_conn.get::<_, Vec<u8>>(cache_key.clone()).await {\n        if !cached.is_empty() {\n            debug!(\"cache hit\");\n            let value: Paginated<LedgerEntry> = serde_json::from_slice(&cached)?;\n            return Ok(Json(value));\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Cache miss \u2013 fetching from service layer\n    let result = state.query_service.query_entries(filter, pagination).await?;\n\n    // Store in cache \u2013 set TTL 60s\n    let ttl_seconds = 60;\n    if let Ok(serialized) = serde_json::to_vec(&result) {\n        let _: () = redis_conn.set_ex(cache_key, serialized, ttl_seconds).await?;\n    }\n\n    Ok(Json(result))\n}\n```\n\n### Response Cache Configuration (config.txt)\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/config.txt\n// Lines: 197-209\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)]\npub struct ResponseCacheConfig {\n    #[serde(default)]\n    pub enabled: bool,\n    #[serde(default = \"default_cache_duration\")]\n    pub duration: Duration,\n    #[serde(default)]\n    pub respect_cache_control_header: bool,\n}\n\nfn default_cache_duration() -> Duration {\n    Duration::from_secs(5 * 60) // 5 minutes\n}\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Architectural Overview\n\nThe LedgerLink Nexus microservice follows a CQRS (Command Query Responsibility Segregation) inspired architecture with:\n\n1. **View Models (DTOs)**: `LedgerEntryDto`, `LedgerEntryView`, `Paginated<T>`\n2. **Domain Models**: `LedgerEntry`, `AccountSnapshot`\n3. **Repository Layer**: Abstractions like `LedgerEntryRepository` with PostgreSQL implementations\n4. **Service Layer**: Query services that orchestrate caching and repository access\n5. **Response Caching**: Redis-backed caching with configurable TTLs (ranging from 15 seconds to 5 minutes)\n\n### Component Interactions\n\nThe **read path** flows as follows:\n1. HTTP Handler (e.g., `get_ledger_entries` in module_26) receives request\n2. Cache key is generated from tenant ID + query parameters\n3. Redis cache is checked first (`cache.get()`)\n4. On cache miss, the repository fetches from PostgreSQL\n5. Response is serialized and stored in Redis with TTL (`set_ex`)\n\nThe **write path** flows as follows:\n1. Write handler/service receives mutation request\n2. Database INSERT/UPDATE is executed within a transaction\n3. **No cache invalidation occurs** - this is the flaw\n\n### Root Cause of Stale Data Issue\n\n**The fundamental architectural flaw is the absence of an invalidation signal from write handlers to the cache layer.**\n\nSpecifically:\n- Read handlers in `module_44`, `module_26`, `module_52`, `module_50`, and `module_55` implement read-through caching with Redis\n- Write handlers in `module_38` execute database INSERTs but do **not** call any cache invalidation method\n- The caching module (`module_9`) has a `purge_namespace()` method designed exactly for this purpose, but it is never invoked by write operations\n- The cache entries persist until their TTL expires (60 seconds to 5 minutes depending on configuration)\n\nThis creates a window where:\n1. Client A reads ledger entries \u2192 cached\n2. Client B updates a ledger entry \u2192 DB updated, cache NOT invalidated\n3. Client A reads ledger entries again \u2192 receives stale cached data\n4. Only after TTL expiration does Client A see the updated data\n\n### Comparison with module_67\n\nInterestingly, `module_67` shows a partial attempt at cache invalidation in `create_entry()`:\n\n```rust\n// module_67.txt lines 264-270\n// Invalidate parent list (simple strategy: delete entire key space).\nlet mut conn = self.redis.get_async_connection().await?;\nlet pattern = format!(\"tenant:{}:ledger_entry:*\", entry.tenant_id);\nlet _: () = redis::cmd(\"UNLINK\").arg(pattern).query_async(&mut conn).await?;\n```\n\nHowever, this invalidates **individual entry caches** (key pattern `tenant:{id}:ledger_entry:*`) but NOT the **paginated list caches** which use different key patterns like:\n- `ledger_entries:{tenant}:{filter}:{page}:{per_page}` (module_44)\n- `ledger:v1:tenant={tenant}:page={page}:size={size}` (module_72)\n- `ledger_entries:v1:{tenant}:{page}:{per_page}:...` (module_26)\n\n## Implementation\n\n### Proposed Solution: Explicit Cache Invalidation Pattern\n\nThe recommended architectural solution is **explicit cache invalidation** (also known as cache-aside with write-through invalidation).\n\n**Design Pattern**: After each successful database write operation, the write handler must explicitly signal the cache layer to invalidate all affected cache entries.\n\n**Justification for this approach over alternatives**:\n\n1. **Why not just lower the cache TTL?**\n   - Reducing TTL (e.g., to 1 second) would severely impact performance and defeat the purpose of caching\n   - Still creates a consistency window, just smaller\n   - Does not scale - you cannot tune TTL per mutation type\n\n2. **Why not write-through caching?**\n   - Write-through would require updating all possible cache keys on every write\n   - Pagination makes this impractical (would need to update N page variations)\n   - More complex to implement correctly\n\n3. **Why explicit invalidation is superior**:\n   - Immediate consistency after mutations\n   - Targeted - only invalidates relevant cache entries\n   - Maintains high cache hit rates for unchanged data\n   - Aligns with existing `purge_namespace()` infrastructure\n\n### Modules Requiring Modification\n\n1. **Write Handler Module (module_38.txt)**\n   - The `insert()` method needs to accept a cache reference and call invalidation\n\n2. **Caching Service Module (module_9.txt or module_72.txt)**\n   - Already has `purge_namespace()` and `purge()` methods - these need to be exposed/called\n\n3. **Service Layer Modules (module_44.txt, module_52.txt, module_50.txt)**\n   - Write operations need to coordinate with the response cache\n\n### New Interactions Required\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510         \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510         \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502  Write Handler  \u2502\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u25b6\u2502  Database Layer  \u2502\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u25b6\u2502  PostgreSQL \u2502\n\u2502  (module_38)    \u2502         \u2502  (Repository)    \u2502         \u2502             \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518         \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518         \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n         \u2502\n         \u2502 On Success\n         \u25bc\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510         \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502  Cache Service  \u2502\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u25b6\u2502     Redis        \u2502\n\u2502  (module_9)     \u2502 DELETE  \u2502                  \u2502\n\u2502  invalidate()   \u2502 keys    \u2502                  \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518         \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n```\n\n### Implementation Outline\n\n1. **Modify write handlers to inject cache service**:\n```rust\n// In module_38.txt - add cache dependency\npub struct LedgerEntryPgRepository {\n    pool: PgPool,\n    cache: ResponseCache,  // NEW: inject cache service\n}\n\nimpl LedgerEntryPgRepository {\n    pub async fn insert(&self, entry: &LedgerEntry) -> Result<(), PaginationError> {\n        // ... existing INSERT logic ...\n\n        tx.commit().await?;\n\n        // NEW: Invalidate paginated response cache for this tenant/account\n        let namespace = format!(\"ledger_entries:{}\", entry.account_id);\n        self.cache.purge_namespace(&namespace).await?;\n\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n```\n\n2. **Ensure cache key patterns are consistent**:\n   - Read handlers and invalidation logic must use matching key patterns\n   - Consider using a shared `CacheKey` builder to ensure consistency\n\n3. **Add invalidation to all write paths**:\n   - INSERT operations\n   - UPDATE operations\n   - DELETE operations\n   - Bulk/batch operations\n\n## Summary\n\n- **Primary finding**: The stale data issue is caused by the **absence of cache invalidation signals** from write handlers to the Redis response cache. Write operations modify the PostgreSQL database but do not notify the caching layer, leaving cached responses stale until TTL expiration.\n\n- **Key components**:\n  - **Caching Module**: `module_9.txt` (core ResponseCache), `module_44.txt`, `module_72.txt`\n  - **Read Handlers**: `module_26.txt` (actix-web GET endpoint), `module_52.txt`, `module_44.txt` (Axum)\n  - **Write Handlers**: `module_38.txt` (insert without invalidation)\n  - **Configuration**: `config.txt` (ResponseCacheConfig with 5-minute default TTL)\n\n- **Architectural pattern**: The system uses a **cache-aside (lazy loading)** pattern for reads but lacks the corresponding **cache invalidation** on writes. The fix requires implementing **explicit cache invalidation** by having write handlers call the existing `purge_namespace()` or `purge()` methods in the cache service after successful database mutations.\n\n- **Recommendations**:\n  1. Modify `module_38.txt` write handlers to call cache invalidation after DB commits\n  2. Ensure consistent cache key generation between read and write paths\n  3. Use the existing `purge_namespace()` method in `module_9.txt` for targeted invalidation\n  4. Consider adding a dedicated `CacheInvalidator` service to centralize invalidation logic\n  5. Add tracing/metrics to track cache invalidation events for observability\n",

Useful when a ledger\n    /// mutation happens and cached projections must be invalidated.\n    #[instrument(skip(self))]\n    pub async fn purge_namespace(&self, namespace: &str) -> Result<u64, CacheError> {\n        let pattern = format!(\"{}:{}:*\", self.prefix, namespace);\n        let mut conn = self.conn.write().await;\n        // NOTE: SCAN could be more graceful for prod, kept simple here.\n        let keys: Vec<String> = conn.keys(pattern).await?;\n        let deleted: u64 = conn.del(keys).await?;\n        debug!(\"purged {} stale cache entries under '{}'\", deleted, namespace);\n        Ok(deleted)\n    }\n```\n\n### Read Handler with Caching (module_44.txt)\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/module_44.txt\n// Lines: 355-408\n\n    #[instrument(skip(self))]\n    pub async fn list(\n        &self,\n        tenant: Uuid,\n        query: ListQuery,\n    ) -> Result<Paginated<LedgerEntryDto>, ServiceError> {\n        // 1. Try cache (30ms timeout to avoid head-of-line blocking)\n        let key = Self::cache_key(tenant, &query);\n        if let Ok(Some(raw)) = self.try_fetch_cache(&key).await {\n            debug!(%tenant, %key, \"Cache hit\");\n            return serde_json::from_slice::<Paginated<LedgerEntryDto>>(&raw)\n                .map_err(ServiceError::CacheSerialization);\n        }\n\n        // 2. Query repository\n        debug!(%tenant, \"Cache miss \u2013 querying DB\");\n        let (entries, total) = self.repo.list(tenant, &query).await?;\n        // ... builds paginated response ...\n\n        // 3. Backfill cache (best-effort)\n        let _ = self.persist_cache(&key, &payload).await;\n\n        Ok(payload)\n    }\n\n    async fn persist_cache<T: Serialize>(&self, key: &str, value: &T) -> Result<(), ServiceError> {\n        let mut conn: RedisConn = self.redis.get().await?;\n        let data = serde_json::to_vec(value)?;\n        let _: () = conn\n            .set_ex(key, data, 60) // 60 seconds TTL\n            .await\n            .map_err(ServiceError::Cache)?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n```\n\n### Write Handler WITHOUT Cache Invalidation (module_38.txt)\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/module_38.txt\n// Lines: 282-306\n\n/// An *idempotent* command that inserts a ledger entry inside its own\n/// transaction.  Exposed as a convenience; not part of the trait.\n///\n/// Demonstrates how we keep read & write paths separated (`CQRS` style).\nimpl LedgerEntryPgRepository {\n    #[instrument(skip_all, name = \"repo.ledger.insert\")]\n    pub async fn insert(&self, entry: &LedgerEntry) -> Result<(), PaginationError> {\n        let mut tx = self.pool.begin().await?;\n\n        sqlx::query(\n            r#\"\n            INSERT INTO ledger_entries\n            (id, account_id, amount, currency, description, created_at)\n            VALUES ($1, $2, $3, $4, $5, $6)\n            ON CONFLICT (id) DO NOTHING\n            \"#,\n        )\n        .bind(entry.id)\n        .bind(entry.account_id)\n        .bind(entry.amount)\n        .bind(&entry.currency)\n        .bind(&entry.description)\n        .bind(entry.created_at)\n        .execute(&mut tx)\n        .await?;\n\n        tx.commit().await?;\n        Ok(())\n        // NOTE: NO CACHE INVALIDATION IS PERFORMED HERE\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Read Handler with Response Caching (module_26.txt)\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/module_26.txt\n// Lines: 317-386\n\n#[get(\"/api/v1/ledger/entries\")]\n#[instrument(skip(dto, state, auth), fields(tenant = %auth.tenant_id))]\npub async fn get_ledger_entries(\n    auth: AuthContext,\n    Query(dto): Query<LedgerEntryQueryDto>,\n    state: Data<AppState>,\n) -> Result<Json<Paginated<LedgerEntry>>, ApiError> {\n    // ... validation ...\n\n    let cache_key = make_cache_key(&auth.tenant_id, &dto);\n\n    // Attempt cache hit\n    if let Ok(cached) = redis_conn.get::<_, Vec<u8>>(cache_key.clone()).await {\n        if !cached.is_empty() {\n            debug!(\"cache hit\");\n            let value: Paginated<LedgerEntry> = serde_json::from_slice(&cached)?;\n            return Ok(Json(value));\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Cache miss \u2013 fetching from service layer\n    let result = state.query_service.query_entries(filter, pagination).await?;\n\n    // Store in cache \u2013 set TTL 60s\n    let ttl_seconds = 60;\n    if let Ok(serialized) = serde_json::to_vec(&result) {\n        let _: () = redis_conn.set_ex(cache_key, serialized, ttl_seconds).await?;\n    }\n\n    Ok(Json(result))\n}\n```\n\n### Response Cache Configuration (config.txt)\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/config.txt\n// Lines: 197-209\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)]\npub struct ResponseCacheConfig {\n    #[serde(default)]\n    pub enabled: bool,\n    #[serde(default = \"default_cache_duration\")]\n    pub duration: Duration,\n    #[serde(default)]\n    pub respect_cache_control_header: bool,\n}\n\nfn default_cache_duration() -> Duration {\n    Duration::from_secs(5 * 60) // 5 minutes\n}\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Architectural Overview\n\nThe LedgerLink Nexus microservice follows a CQRS (Command Query Responsibility Segregation) inspired architecture with:\n\n1. **View Models (DTOs)**: `LedgerEntryDto`, `LedgerEntryView`, `Paginated<T>`\n2. **Domain Models**: `LedgerEntry`, `AccountSnapshot`\n3. **Repository Layer**: Abstractions like `LedgerEntryRepository` with PostgreSQL implementations\n4. **Service Layer**: Query services that orchestrate caching and repository access\n5. **Response Caching**: Redis-backed caching with configurable TTLs (ranging from 15 seconds to 5 minutes)\n\n### Component Interactions\n\nThe **read path** flows as follows:\n1. HTTP Handler (e.g., `get_ledger_entries` in module_26) receives request\n2. Cache key is generated from tenant ID + query parameters\n3. Redis cache is checked first (`cache.get()`)\n4. On cache miss, the repository fetches from PostgreSQL\n5. Response is serialized and stored in Redis with TTL (`set_ex`)\n\nThe **write path** flows as follows:\n1. Write handler/service receives mutation request\n2. Database INSERT/UPDATE is executed within a transaction\n3. **No cache invalidation occurs** - this is the flaw\n\n### Root Cause of Stale Data Issue\n\n**The fundamental architectural flaw is the absence of an invalidation signal from write handlers to the cache layer.**\n\nSpecifically:\n- Read handlers in `module_44`, `module_26`, `module_52`, `module_50`, and `module_55` implement read-through caching with Redis\n- Write handlers in `module_38` execute database INSERTs but do **not** call any cache invalidation method\n- The caching module (`module_9`) has a `purge_namespace()` method designed exactly for this purpose, but it is never invoked by write operations\n- The cache entries persist until their TTL expires (60 seconds to 5 minutes depending on configuration)\n\nThis creates a window where:\n1. Client A reads ledger entries \u2192 cached\n2. Client B updates a ledger entry \u2192 DB updated, cache NOT invalidated\n3. Client A reads ledger entries again \u2192 receives stale cached data\n4. Only after TTL expiration does Client A see the updated data\n\n### Comparison with module_67\n\nInterestingly, `module_67` shows a partial attempt at cache invalidation in `create_entry()`:\n\n```rust\n// module_67.txt lines 264-270\n// Invalidate parent list (simple strategy: delete entire key space).\nlet mut conn = self.redis.get_async_connection().await?;\nlet pattern = format!(\"tenant:{}:ledger_entry:*\", entry.tenant_id);\nlet _: () = redis::cmd(\"UNLINK\").arg(pattern).query_async(&mut conn).await?;\n```\n\nHowever, this invalidates **individual entry caches** (key pattern `tenant:{id}:ledger_entry:*`) but NOT the **paginated list caches** which use different key patterns like:\n- `ledger_entries:{tenant}:{filter}:{page}:{per_page}` (module_44)\n- `ledger:v1:tenant={tenant}:page={page}:size={size}` (module_72)\n- `ledger_entries:v1:{tenant}:{page}:{per_page}:...` (module_26)\n\n## Implementation\n\n### Proposed Solution: Explicit Cache Invalidation Pattern\n\nThe recommended architectural solution is **explicit cache invalidation** (also known as cache-aside with write-through invalidation).\n\n**Design Pattern**: After each successful database write operation, the write handler must explicitly signal the cache layer to invalidate all affected cache entries.\n\n**Justification for this approach over alternatives**:\n\n1. **Why not just lower the cache TTL?**\n   - Reducing TTL (e.g., to 1 second) would severely impact performance and defeat the purpose of caching\n   - Still creates a consistency window, just smaller\n   - Does not scale - you cannot tune TTL per mutation type\n\n2. **Why not write-through caching?**\n   - Write-through would require updating all possible cache keys on every write\n   - Pagination makes this impractical (would need to update N page variations)\n   - More complex to implement correctly\n\n3. **Why explicit invalidation is superior**:\n   - Immediate consistency after mutations\n   - Targeted - only invalidates relevant cache entries\n   - Maintains high cache hit rates for unchanged data\n   - Aligns with existing `purge_namespace()` infrastructure\n\n### Modules Requiring Modification\n\n1. **Write Handler Module (module_38.txt)**\n   - The `insert()` method needs to accept a cache reference and call invalidation\n\n2. **Caching Service Module (module_9.txt or module_72.txt)**\n   - Already has `purge_namespace()` and `purge()` methods - these need to be exposed/called\n\n3. **Service Layer Modules (module_44.txt, module_52.txt, module_50.txt)**\n   - Write operations need to coordinate with the response cache\n\n### New Interactions Required\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510         \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510         \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502  Write Handler  \u2502\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u25b6\u2502  Database Layer  \u2502\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u25b6\u2502  PostgreSQL \u2502\n\u2502  (module_38)    \u2502         \u2502  (Repository)    \u2502         \u2502             \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518 \u25bc\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510         \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502  Cache Service  \u2502\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u25b6\u2502     Redis        \u2502\n\u2502  (module_9)     \u2502 DELETE  \u2502                  \u2502\n\u2502  invalidate()   \u2502 keys    \u2502                  \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518         \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n```\n\n### Implementation Outline\n\n1. **Modify write handlers to inject cache service**:\n```rust\n// In module_38.txt - add cache dependency\npub struct LedgerEntryPgRepository {\n    pool: PgPool,\n    cache: ResponseCache,  // NEW: inject cache service\n}\n\nimpl LedgerEntryPgRepository {\n    pub async fn insert(&self, entry: &LedgerEntry) -> Result<(), PaginationError> {\n        // ... existing INSERT logic ...\n\n        tx.commit().await?;\n\n        // NEW: Invalidate paginated response cache for this tenant/account\n        let namespace = format!(\"ledger_entries:{}\", entry.account_id);\n        self.cache.purge_namespace(&namespace).await?;\n\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n```\n\n2. **Ensure cache key patterns are consistent**:\n   - Read handlers and invalidation logic must use matching key patterns\n   - Consider using a shared `CacheKey` builder to ensure consistency\n\n3. **Add invalidation to all write paths**:\n   - INSERT operations\n   - UPDATE operations\n   - DELETE operations\n   - Bulk/batch operations\n\n## Summary\n\n- **Primary finding**: The stale data issue is caused by the **absence of cache invalidation signals** from write handlers to the Redis response cache. Write operations modify the PostgreSQL database but do not notify the caching layer, leaving cached responses stale until TTL expiration.\n\n- **Key components**:\n  - **Caching Module**: `module_9.txt` (core ResponseCache), `module_44.txt`, `module_72.txt`\n  - **Read Handlers**: `module_26.txt` (actix-web GET endpoint), `module_52.txt`, `module_44.txt` (Axum)\n  - **Write Handlers**: `module_38.txt` (insert without invalidation)\n  - **Configuration**: `config.txt` (ResponseCacheConfig with 5-minute default TTL)\n\n- **Architectural pattern**: The system uses a **cache-aside (lazy loading)** pattern for reads but lacks the corresponding **cache invalidation** on writes. The fix requires implementing **explicit cache invalidation** by having write handlers call the existing `purge_namespace()` or `purge()` methods in the cache service after successful database mutations.\n\n- **Recommendations**:\n  1. Modify `module_38.txt` write handlers to call cache invalidation after DB commits\n  2. Ensure consistent cache key generation between read and write paths\n  3. Use the existing `purge_namespace()` method in `module_9.txt` for targeted invalidation\n  4. Consider adding a dedicated `CacheInvalidator` service to centralize invalidation logic\n  5. Add tracing/metrics to track cache invalidation events for observability\n",

# Solution: rust_api_microservice_expert_008_architectural_understanding_expert_01

## Key Files Identified

### Caching Modules
- `/app/project/src/module_9.txt` - Core response cache layer with `ResponseCache::purge_namespace()` invalidation method
- `/app/project/src/module_44.txt` - Ledger Entry listing with Redis response-level caching (read handler)
- `/app/project/src/module_72.txt` - Pagination + Response Caching facade with `purge()` method

### Read Handler Modules (GET Operations)
- `/app/project/src/module_26.txt` - Ledger Entry Query Endpoint using actix-web with `#[get("/api/v1/ledger/entries")]` route
- `/app/project/src/module_52.txt` - High-frequency paginated read-model with Redis response-caching via `LedgerEntryService`
- `/app/project/src/module_44.txt` - Ledger Entry listing via `list_ledger_entries_handler` with Axum

### Write Handler Modules (INSERT/UPDATE Operations)
- `/app/project/src/module_38.txt` - Contains `insert()` method that writes to DB without cache invalidation
- `/app/project/src/module_67.txt` - `LedgerEntryService::create_entry()` with partial cache invalidation (only individual entry cache, not paginated response cache)

### Configuration
- `/app/project/src/config.txt` - Contains `ResponseCacheConfig` with `duration` (default 5 minutes TTL) and `enabled` flag
